<p><b>Dalian</b> is a major city and <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">seaport</a> in the south of <a href="/wiki/Liaoning" title="Liaoning">Liaoning Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. It is the southernmost city of <a href="/wiki/Northeast_China" title="Northeast China">Northeast China</a> and at the tip of the <a href="/wiki/Liaodong_Peninsula" title="Liaodong Peninsula">Liaodong Peninsula</a>. Dalian is the province's second largest city and has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city" title="Sub-provincial city">sub-provincial</a> administrative status;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> only the provincial capital (<a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a>) is larger. The <a href="/wiki/Shandong_Peninsula" title="Shandong Peninsula">Shandong Peninsula</a> lies southwest across the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bohai_Strait" title="Bohai Strait">Bohai Strait</a>; <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> lies across the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">Yellow Sea</a> to the east.</p>
<p>Today, a financial, shipping and logistics centre for <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Asia" title="Northeast Asia">Northeast Asia</a>, Dalian has a significant history of being used by foreign powers for its ports. Dalian was previously known as both <b><a href="/wiki/Russian_Dalian" title="Russian Dalian">Dalniy</a></b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Дальний</span>; <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="[[:Template:ISO 639 name ru-latin]] transliteration"><i><b>Dal'nii</b></i></span>) and <b><a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Leased_Territory" title="Kwantung Leased Territory">Dairen</a></b> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span lang="ja">大連</span>). However the city was better known as <b>Port Arthur</b> (Russian: <span lang="ru">Порт-Артур</span>; <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Russian transliteration"><i><b>Port-Artur</b></i></span>) and <b>Ryojun</b> (Japanese: <span lang="ja">旅順</span>) from the original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lushun" title="Lushun">Port Arthur</a>, now the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshunkou" title="Lüshunkou">Lüshunkou</a> district.</p>
<p>In 2016, Dalian ranks 31st in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a> published by the <a href="/wiki/Z/Yen" title="Z/Yen">Z/Yen Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Financial_Centre" title="Qatar Financial Centre">Qatar Financial Centre Authority</a>, the other Chinese cities on the list being <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">Qingdao</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GFCI_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-GFCI-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2012, Dalian ranked 82nd in the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Global_City_Competitiveness_Index" title="Global city">Global City Competitiveness Index</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a> (<a href="/wiki/Economist_Group" title="Economist Group">The Economist Group</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In 2006, Dalian was named China's most livable city by <i><a href="/wiki/China_Daily" title="China Daily">China Daily</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Modern Dalian originated from <b>Qingniwa</b> (Chinese: <span lang="zh">青泥洼</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Qīngníwā</span></i>; literally: "cyan mud swamp") or <a href="/wiki/Qingniwaqiao" title="Qingniwaqiao">Qingniwaqiao</a> (Chinese: <span lang="zh">青泥洼桥</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Qīngníwāqiáo</span></i>; literally: "bridge over the cyan mud swamp"), a small fishing village. Russia built a commercial town for the <a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Leased_Territory" title="Kwantung Leased Territory">Kwantung Leased Territory</a> after <a href="/wiki/Russian_Dalian" title="Russian Dalian">assuming control</a> in 1898 and called it "Dalniy" (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Дальний <i>Dal'nii</i></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'a remote one (in reference to the town's location)',<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> rendered as Chinese: <span lang="zh">达里尼</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Dálǐní</span></i>) from 1898–1905. After the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a>, Japan occupied the Kwantung Leased Territory and renamed the city Dairen <span style="font-weight: normal">(<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">大連/だいれん</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> after the Chinese name for <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Bay" title="Dalian Bay">Dalian Bay</a> (simplified Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">大连湾</span>; traditional Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">大連灣</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Dàlián Wān</span></i>). English sources called the city "Dairen" in this period, from the Japanese.</p>
<p>In 1950, Dalian merged with nearby town called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshun" title="Lüshun">Lüshun</a> (Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">旅顺</span>) (formerly "Ryojun" and before that, "Port Arthur") to form the city of <b>Lüda</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> (Chinese: <span lang="zh">旅大</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Lǚdà</span></i>), a name formed from the first syllable of each constituent's name which was usually rendered as <b>Luta</b> in English during that era. In 1981, the <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="State Council of the People's Republic of China">State Council</a> again renamed the city, from Lüda to "Dalian" (simplified Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hans">大连</span>; traditional Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">大連</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Dàlián</span></i>, the same Chinese characters as Japanese <i>Dairen</i>), effective 5 March 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qin_Dynasty" title="Qin Dynasty">Qin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" title="Han Dynasty">Han</a> periods (221 BC–AD 220), Chinese expanded their territories into northern <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> through the Dalian region, then under the jurisdiction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liaodong" title="Liaodong">Liaodong</a> county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Kingdoms" title="Sixteen Kingdoms">Sixteen Kingdoms</a> era (3rd through 5th centuries), the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Goguryeo" title="Goguryeo">Goguryeo</a> controlled this region. In the early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a> (618–907), the Dalian region was part of <a href="/wiki/Andong" title="Andong">Andong</a> Prefecture in Jili state; during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liao_Dynasty" title="Liao Dynasty">Liao Dynasty</a> (916–1125), it was part of Dong Jing Tong Liaoyang county. Dalian was named Sanshan in the period of <a href="/wiki/Cao_Wei" title="Cao Wei">Wei</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jin_Dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin Dynasty (265–420)">Jin</a> (220–420), San Shanpu in the Tang Dynasty (618–907), Sanshan Seaport in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a> (1368–1644), and Qingniwakou during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> (1644–1911).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qing_Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Qing Dynasty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1880s, Jinzhou, the north of downtown within Dalian, now <a href="/wiki/Jinzhou_District" title="Jinzhou District">Jinzhou District</a>, was a walled town and centre for political intrigue and economic activity. The Qing government built bridges and heavily fortified the peninsula. Mining camps on the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Bay" title="Dalian Bay">Dalian Bay</a> became the small town of Qingniwa or <a href="/wiki/Qingniwaqiao" title="Qingniwaqiao">Qingniwaqiao</a>, near what became downtown Dalian.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British.2C_Russian.2C_and_Japanese_occupations">British, Russian, and Japanese occupations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: British, Russian, and Japanese occupations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Dalian" title="Russian Dalian">Russian Dalian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Leased_Territory" title="Kwantung Leased Territory">Kwantung Leased Territory</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">

</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg/220px-Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg/330px-Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg/440px-Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dalian_Hotel_%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%AE%BE%E9%A6%86.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dalian Hotel, formerly <a href="/wiki/Yamato_Hotel" title="Yamato Hotel">Yamato Hotel</a>, was built in 1914</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The British occupied Qingniwa in 1858,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> but it returned to Chinese control in the 1880s. Port Arthur at the peninsula's tip took its English name from Royal Navy Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/William_C._Arthur" title="William C. Arthur">William C. Arthur</a>, but Chinese called it <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshun" title="Lüshun">Lüshun</a>. Although China heavily fortified the area, in which it allowed trade with foreigners, Japan swiftly overcame those defenses<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a>, committing the <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur_massacre_(China)" title="Port Arthur massacre (China)">Port Arthur massacre</a> during the war in November 1894. In April 1895, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> conceded defeat in the First Sino-Japanese War, ceding <a href="/wiki/Liaodong_Peninsula" title="Liaodong Peninsula">Liaodong Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penghu" title="Penghu">Penghu</a>, and making many other concessions in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Shimonoseki" title="Treaty of Shimonoseki">Treaty of Shimonoseki</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Triple_Intervention" title="Triple Intervention">Triple Intervention</a> by Russia, France and Germany forced Japan to return the <a href="/wiki/Liaodong_Peninsula" title="Liaodong Peninsula">Liaodong Peninsula</a> to China, despite the treaty's terms; instead the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> coerced a lease of the peninsula from the Qing Dynasty in 1898. For Russia the region of the peninsula was of particular interest as one of the few areas in the region that had the potential to develop <a href="/wiki/Port#Warm-water_port" title="Port">ice-free ports</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The Russians built a modern commercial port city, which they wanted to become the Paris of the Far East, and called it Dal'niy (Russian: <span lang="ru">Дальний</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Linked to the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>'s branch line from <a href="/wiki/Harbin" title="Harbin">Harbin</a>, Dalniy became Russia's primary port-city in Asia, and also served other western traders. Russia signed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pavlov_Agreement_(1898)" title="Pavlov Agreement (1898)">Pavlov Agreement (1898)</a> with China, which granted Russia a 25-year lease on Dalian and Lüshun and exclusive right to lay a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Eastern_Railway" title="Chinese Eastern Railway">Chinese Eastern Railway</a>—what would become the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Manchurian_Railway" title="South Manchurian Railway">South Manchurian Railway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Russia spent more than 10 million golden rubles (equivalent to 11.5 billion of today's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rubles" title="Rubles">rubles</a>) building the new ice-free port city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Russia heavily fortified both Dalniy (Qingniwaqiao of Zhongshan District) and the Port Arthur naval base (Lüshunkou) before and after the <a href="/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion" title="Boxer Rebellion">Boxer Rebellion</a>. Missionaries and converts were killed in the peninsula during the insurrection, although the massive massacres of ethnic Chinese Christians including <a href="/wiki/Metrophanes,_Chi_Sung" title="Metrophanes, Chi Sung">Metrophanes, Chi Sung</a> occurred at <a href="/wiki/Harbin" title="Harbin">Harbin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orthodox.cn_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Orthodox.cn-16">[16]</a></sup> Also, Western expeditionary forces suppressed the Boxers across the Yellow Sea in <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a>.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a>, the peninsula became a major battleground. Major-General Baron <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatoly_Stoessel" title="Anatoly Stoessel">Anatoly Stoessel</a> defended the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Arthur" title="Siege of Port Arthur">siege of Port Arthur</a>, for five months, but the Japanese army managed to sink several Russian ships attempting to relieve him through long-distance fire in early December. Admiral Eugene Alexeyeff was blamed for splitting precious resources shipped 5,000 miles (8,047 km) across the single tracked Trans-Siberian Railway and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchurian_Railway" title="Manchurian Railway">Manchurian Railway</a> between Dalniy and Port Arthur. After the Japanese navy crippled the remaining Russian battleship <i><a href="/wiki/Russian_battleship_Sevastopol_(1895)" title="Russian battleship Sevastopol (1895)">Sevastopol</a></i> in three weeks of constant attacks, and explosives detonated in tunnels destroyed Port Arthur's remaining defenses at year's end, Russia surrendered the port on 2 January 1905.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Portsmouth" title="Treaty of Portsmouth">Treaty of Portsmouth</a> ceded Port Arthur to Japan, which set up the <a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Leased_Territory" title="Kwantung Leased Territory">Kwantung Leased Territory</a> or <i>Guandongzhou</i> (關東州), on roughly the southern half (Jinzhou District and south) of present-day Dalian. Japanese invested heavily in the region, which became the main trading port between Manchuria and Japan. Japan leased the area from <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a> after establishing the puppet state in 1932. In 1937, as the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> began, Japan enlarged and modernized the trade zone as two cities: the northern Dairen (Dalian) and the southern Ryojun (Lüshun or Port Arthur).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II">Post-World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG/220px-China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG/330px-China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG/440px-China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:China_Railways_SY_in_Dalian.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A retired <a href="/wiki/China_Railways_SY" title="China Railways SY">China Railways SY</a>, built jointly by <a href="/wiki/CNR_Dalian" title="CNR Dalian">Dalian Locomotive Works</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tangshan_Railway_Vehicle" title="Tangshan Railway Vehicle">Tangshan Locomotive Works</a> in 1959, on display in front of Dalian Modern Museum</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the unconditional <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrender of Japan</a> in August 1945, Dairen was passed to the Soviets, whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchurian_Strategic_Offensive_Operation" title="Manchurian Strategic Offensive Operation">Manchurian Strategic Offensive Operation</a> had liberated the city. The Soviets and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Communists" title="Chinese Communists">Chinese Communists</a> cooperated to develop the city, relatively undamaged during the war,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> especially its industrial infrastructure and the port. The Soviet government rented the port and in 1945 the first Chinese Communist mayor of the new Lüda Administrative Office (<span lang="zh-Hans">旅大行政公署</span>) had been appointed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1950, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a> presented the city to the Chinese Communist government without any compensation. Dalian and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshun" title="Lüshun">Lüshun</a> (former Port Arthur) merged as Lüda on 1 December 1950. From 12 March 1953 to 1 August 1954 it was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Direct-controlled municipality of the People's Republic of China">direct-controlled municipality</a> and not part of Liaoning. Soviet troops left the city in 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-6"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> After the Soviets left, the PRC made Lüda a major shipbuilding centre.</p>
<p>In 1981, it was renamed Dalian, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshunkou" title="Lüshunkou">Lüshunkou</a> becoming a constituent district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-7"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1984, the Chinese Government designated the city a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of the People's Republic of China">Special Economic Zone</a>. At the time, Dalian was China's largest foreign trade port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_1990">Post 1990</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post 1990">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E9%9D%92%E6%B3%A5%E6%B4%BC%E6%A1%A5.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3672" data-file-width="4896" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%E9%9D%92%E6%B3%A5%E6%B4%BC%E6%A1%A5.JPG/220px-%E9%9D%92%E6%B3%A5%E6%B4%BC%E6%A1%A5.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%E9%9D%92%E6%B3%A5%E6%B4%BC%E6%A1%A5.JPG/330px-%E9%9D%92%E6%B3%A5%E6%B4%BC%E6%A1%A5.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%E9%9D%92%E6%B3%A5%E6%B4%BC%E6%A1%A5.JPG/440px-%E9%9D%92%E6%B3%A5%E6%B4%BC%E6%A1%A5.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

Modern day <a href="/wiki/Qingniwaqiao" title="Qingniwaqiao">Qingniwaqiao</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shopping_district" title="Shopping district">shopping district</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1998" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg/220px-%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg/330px-%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg/440px-%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A7%E8%BF%9E%E5%B8%82%E4%B8%AD%E5%B1%B1%E8%B7%AF.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Modern day <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Square_(Dalian)" title="Zhongshan Square (Dalian)">Zhongshan Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city was upgraded from a <a href="/wiki/Prefecture-level_city" title="Prefecture-level city">prefecture-level city</a> to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city" title="Sub-provincial city">sub-provincial city</a> in May 1994, with no change in its administrative subdivisions. In the 1990s the city benefited from the attention of <a href="/wiki/Bo_Xilai" title="Bo Xilai">Bo Xilai</a> (later Communist Party head of <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>) who was both the mayor of the city and one of the major leaders in the province, who, among other things, banned motorcycles and planted large, lush parks in the city's many traffic circles. He also preserved much of Dalian's <a href="/wiki/Japanese_architecture" title="Japanese architecture">Japanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_architecture" title="Russian architecture">Russian</a> architectural heritage. He also worked as former <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Commerce_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of Commerce of the People's Republic of China">Minister of Commerce</a> of the PRC.</p>
<p>In 2008, about 1,000 people protested and blocked traffic as a response of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Tibetan_anti-Chinese_protests" title="2008 Tibetan anti-Chinese protests">2008 Tibetan anti-Chinese protests</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and forced the temporary closure of the local <a href="/wiki/Carrefour" title="Carrefour">Carrefour</a> store.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Xingang_Port_oil_spill" title="Xingang Port oil spill">one of the worst recorded oil spills in China's history</a> occurred in Dalian.</p>
<p>Since 2007, Dalian has been hosting the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum#Summer_annual_meeting" title="World Economic Forum">Annual Meeting of the New Champions</a> ("Summer Davos"), organised by the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, in alternating years with <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The venue for the forum is Dalian International Conference Center in Donggang <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">CBD</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_2010">Post 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>14 August 2011 - <a href="/wiki/Dalian_PX_protest" title="Dalian PX protest">Dalian PX protest</a> occurred.</li>
<li>June 2014 - China's tenth national new area, Dalian Jinpu New Area officially established.</li>
<li>14 June 2016 - Dalian taxi incident occurred.</li>
<li>5 August 2016 - Dalian <a href="/wiki/Huabiao" title="Huabiao">Huabiao</a> incident occurred.</li>
</ul>

<p>One of the most heavily developed industrial areas of China, Dalian municipal area today consists of Dalian proper and the smaller <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%BCshunkou" title="Lüshunkou">Lüshunkou</a> (formerly Lüshun city, known in Western and Russian historic references as Port Arthur), about forty <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a> (74 kilometres; 46 miles) farther along the <a href="/wiki/Liaodong_Peninsula" title="Liaodong Peninsula">Liaodong Peninsula</a>. Historical references note that the Russian designed city of Dalniy (Alt. Dalney), on the south side of <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Bay" title="Dalian Bay">Dalian Bay</a> was 40 kilometres (25 miles) from Port Arthur/Lüshun (known today as Lüshunkou or literally, Lüshun Port).</p>
<p>Dalian is located on <a href="/wiki/Korea_Bay" title="Korea Bay">Korea Bay</a> north of the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">Yellow Sea</a> and roughly in the middle of the Liaodong peninsula at its narrowest neck or <a href="/wiki/Isthmus" title="Isthmus">isthmus</a>. With a coastline of 1,906 km (1,184 mi), it governs the majority of the Liaodong Peninsula and about 260 surrounding islands and reefs. It is seated at south-south-west of the <a href="/wiki/Yalu_River" title="Yalu River">Yalu River</a>, and its harbour entrance forms a sub-bay known as <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Bay" title="Dalian Bay">Dalian Bay</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shore_in_Dalian_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Shore_in_Dalian_%282%29.jpg/220px-Shore_in_Dalian_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Shore_in_Dalian_%282%29.jpg/330px-Shore_in_Dalian_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Shore_in_Dalian_%282%29.jpg/440px-Shore_in_Dalian_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dalian has a <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>-influenced <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Dwa</i>), characterised by humid summers due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Asian_monsoon" title="East Asian monsoon">East Asian monsoon</a>, and cold, windy, dry winters that reflect the influence of the vast <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_anticyclone" title="Siberian anticyclone">Siberian anticyclone</a>. Except for winter, the city experiences a one-month seasonal lag due to its position on the Liaodong Peninsula. The monthly 24-hour average temperature ranges from −3.9 °C (25.0 °F) in January to 24.1 °C (75.4 °F) in August. Annual precipitation averages 602 millimetres (23.7 in) but is heavily concentrated in the summer months and can vary greatly from year to year. Due to the coastal location, the mean <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal temperature variation</a> annually is small, at 6.75 °C (12.2 °F). The monthly percent of possible sunshine ranges from 49% in July to 68% in September and October, with 2,740 hours of bright sunshine annually. The annual mean temperature is 10.90 °C (51.6 °F). Extremes since 1951 have ranged from −21.1 °C (−6 °F) on 4 January 1970 to 36.6 °C (98 °F) on 14 July 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autumn_mountain_foliage_in_dalian_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Autumn_mountain_foliage_in_dalian_%282%29.jpg/220px-Autumn_mountain_foliage_in_dalian_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Autumn_mountain_foliage_in_dalian_%282%29.jpg/330px-Autumn_mountain_foliage_in_dalian_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Autumn_mountain_foliage_in_dalian_%282%29.jpg/440px-Autumn_mountain_foliage_in_dalian_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island,_Dalian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island%2C_Dalian.jpg/220px-Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island%2C_Dalian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island%2C_Dalian.jpg/330px-Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island%2C_Dalian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island%2C_Dalian.jpg/440px-Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island%2C_Dalian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xiaoshuikou_%E5%B0%8F%E6%B0%B4%E5%8F%A3_in_Xiaochangshan_Island,_Dalian.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_in_Dalian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1824" data-file-width="2500" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Sunset_in_Dalian.jpg/220px-Sunset_in_Dalian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Sunset_in_Dalian.jpg/330px-Sunset_in_Dalian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Sunset_in_Dalian.jpg/440px-Sunset_in_Dalian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heishijiao_Park,_Dalian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="500" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Heishijiao_Park%2C_Dalian.jpg/220px-Heishijiao_Park%2C_Dalian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Heishijiao_Park%2C_Dalian.jpg/330px-Heishijiao_Park%2C_Dalian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Heishijiao_Park%2C_Dalian.jpg/440px-Heishijiao_Park%2C_Dalian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heishijiao_Park,_Dalian.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seascape at Heishijiao (黑石礁) Geological Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001, The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> awarded the Dalian Municipal Government for its outstanding contribution to the protection of the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average content of the four pollutants in the air reached Class Ⅱ of National Ambient Air Quality Standards and there were 353 days with <a href="/wiki/Air_Pollution_Index" title="Air Pollution Index">Air Pollution Index</a> (API) over Class Ⅱ (Good), including 108 excellent days with Class Ⅰ (Superior).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AQ_Rating_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-AQ_Rating-24">[24]</a></sup> Dalian frequently ranks Grade 2 for air pollution according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Environmental_Protection_Administration" title="State Environmental Protection Administration">State Environmental Protection Administration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> However, the environmental effects of economic growth are of concern, according to Dalian Environmental Protection Agency, during the first half of 2011, respirable particles in the air increased significantly, with an average 40% higher than 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naut_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-naut-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The water quality of offshore marine space remained stable overall. The annual average content of monitoring indicators for water quality met Class-II of the National Seawater Quality Standard, with the exception of Inorganic Nitrogen in <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Bay" title="Dalian Bay">Dalian Bay</a> and the city's southern coast. The water quality of drinking water sources is considered good and complies with Class-III of Environmental Quality Standards for Surface Water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AQ_Rating_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-AQ_Rating-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recent events have had a major environmental impact on the city. In July 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Xingang_Port_oil_spill" title="Xingang Port oil spill">explosion of two petroleum pipelines</a> released 11,000 barrels of oil into the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">Yellow Sea</a>, according to official statements. Rick Steiner, an American marine conservationist working with <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>, says that the figure could be upwards of 400,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> It was reported as the largest oil spill to occur in China,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and involved 2,000 firefighters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The oil spill stretched for at least 50 square kilometres (19 sq mi). 800 fishing boats were mobilized for the cleanup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The incident caused President <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> and Premier <a href="/wiki/Wen_Jiabao" title="Wen Jiabao">Wen Jiabao</a> to intervene, and Vice Premier <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Dejiang" title="Zhang Dejiang">Zhang Dejiang</a> moved in to help direct the rescue work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> A researcher with the China Environmental Science Research Institute, said that "the impact on marine life and on humans – as the pollution enters the food chain – could last 10 years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> This has compounded aquatic pollution, affecting the city's fishing industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naut_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-naut-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2011, a <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">dike</a> protecting the petrochemical Fujia Factory in <a href="/wiki/Jinzhou_District" title="Jinzhou District">Jinzhou District</a> was breached due to a typhoon. Authorities have ordered the plant to be shut down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Around 12,000 residents protested as the factory, which originally was intended to be based in <a href="/wiki/Xiamen" title="Xiamen">Xiamen</a>, did not receive official approval to operate in Dalian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Municipal authorities ruled that the facility must move, leaving taxpayers to pay the expensive cost of relocation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chinadialogue_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-chinadialogue-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Concerns have been raised over mounting traffic due to "bad urban design" and that the growing rate of car ownership is affecting air quality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naut_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-naut-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The United States <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a> have raised concern about rising traffic in Dalian stating that "rapid growth of traffic in Dalian and in similar Chinese cities will repeat the air quality and energy consumption mistakes of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and other U.S. cities, if not better managed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dalian is the second largest city of Liaoning province, after <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a>, the provincial capital. Dalian City is governed by the Dalian Municipal People's Government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_government">Municipal government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Municipal government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The municipal government is located in the main building on the north side of People's Square on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Road" title="Zhongshan Road">Zhongshan Road</a>, originally built as the Administrative Office of <a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Leased_Territory" title="Kwantung Leased Territory">Kwantung Leased Territory</a>, and other buildings in downtown Dalian. There are the Commerce, Foreign Economy &amp; Trade, Hygiene, Information Industry, Police, Religion, Science &amp; Technology, Transportation and other city-level bureaus, which work closely with the corresponding agencies at the district level.</p>
<p>There are, in addition, 4 national leading open zones (<span lang="zh-Hans">对外开放先导区</span>):</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalian_Development_Zone" title="Dalian Development Zone">The Development Zone</a> (<span lang="zh-hans-CN">开发区</span>)</li>
<li>The Free Trade Zone (<span lang="zh-hans-CN">保税区</span>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dalian_Hi-Tech_Zone" title="Dalian Hi-Tech Zone">The Hi-Tech Industrial Zone</a> (<span lang="zh-hans-CN">高新技术产业园区</span>)</li>
<li>The Jīnshítān (<i>"Golden Pebble Beach"</i>) National Holiday Resort (<span lang="zh-hans-CN">金石滩国家旅游度假区</span>)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>(see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Administrative divisions of the People's Republic of China">Administrative divisions of the People's Republic of China</a>)</p>
<p>The city administers 7 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_of_China" title="District of China">districts</a>, 2 <a href="/wiki/County-level_city" title="County-level city">county-level cities</a>, and 1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" title="County (People's Republic of China)">county</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li>There are 92 sub-districts and 69 towns and townships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-08Yearbook_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-08Yearbook-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>Zhongshan, Xigang, Shahekou and Ganjingzi Districts make up the urban core. Changhai County is made up entirely of islands east of the peninsula.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The population of Dalian according to the 2010 census totaled 6.69 million. The total registered population on household at year end 2014 was 5.943 million, with a net increase of 29,000 over the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stats_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-stats-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg/220px-Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg/330px-Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg/440px-Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wang_Jianlin_-_Annual_Meeting_of_the_New_Champions_Dalian_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wang_Jianlin" title="Wang Jianlin">Wang Jianlin</a>, Chairman of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalian_Wanda_Group" title="Dalian Wanda Group">Dalian Wanda Group</a>, at the Annual Meeting of the New Champions of <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, Dalian 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Dalian" title="Economy of Dalian">Economy of Dalian</a></div>
<p>The city has had a continuous annual double-digit percentage increase in GDP since 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbm_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbm-41">[41]</a></sup> In 2014, the city's GDP registered a 5.8% increase, reaching RMB 765.56 billion, while per capita GDP hit RMB 109,939.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stats_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-stats-1">[1]</a></sup> According to a nationwide appraisal by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Bureau_of_Statistics_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="National Bureau of Statistics of the People's Republic of China">National Bureau of Statistics</a>, Dalian ranks eighth among Chinese cities in terms of overall strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbm_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-cbm-41">[41]</a></sup> The city’s main industries include machine manufacturing, petrochemicals and oil refining, and electronics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_view_on_Renmin_Road,_Dalian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Street_view_on_Renmin_Road%2C_Dalian.jpg/220px-Street_view_on_Renmin_Road%2C_Dalian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Street_view_on_Renmin_Road%2C_Dalian.jpg/330px-Street_view_on_Renmin_Road%2C_Dalian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Street_view_on_Renmin_Road%2C_Dalian.jpg/440px-Street_view_on_Renmin_Road%2C_Dalian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_view_on_Renmin_Road,_Dalian.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Street view on Renmin Road, Dalian</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_aquaculture">Agriculture and aquaculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Agriculture and aquaculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dalian was originally an agriculture and aquaculture-based area, which, after the opening of the ferry between <a href="/wiki/Yantai" title="Yantai">Yantai</a> and Lüshun during the early 20th century, began to be populated by the farmers and fishers of <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a>, across the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">Yellow Sea</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Chuang_Guandong" title="Chuang Guandong">Chuang Guandong</a> (闯关东) era.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heavy.2C_light_and_distribution_industries">Heavy, light and distribution industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Heavy, light and distribution industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Varyag_during_refitting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="720" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Varyag_during_refitting.jpg/220px-Varyag_during_refitting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Varyag_during_refitting.jpg/330px-Varyag_during_refitting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Varyag_during_refitting.jpg/440px-Varyag_during_refitting.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Varyag_during_refitting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ex-<i>Varyag</i> undergoing refit in <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Shipbuilding_Industry_Company" title="Dalian Shipbuilding Industry Company">Dalian Shipbuilding Industry Company</a> (2011), which later became China's first <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Chinese_aircraft_carrier_Liaoning" title="Chinese aircraft carrier Liaoning">Liaoning</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Even before and during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a>, the shipbuilding and locomotives industries were located in the city such as the companies which later became <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Shipbuilding_Industry_Company" title="Dalian Shipbuilding Industry Company">Dalian Shipbuilding Industry Company</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalian_locomotive_works" title="Dalian locomotive works">CNR Dalian Locomotive &amp; Rolling Stock Works (DLoco)</a>. After the WWII, Dalian became an important centre of the heavy and light industries, including companies such as Dalian Heavy Industry Co., Dalian Chemical Group, and Wafangdian Bearing Co.; and of the distribution industry, such as the <a href="/wiki/Dashang_Group" title="Dashang Group">Dashang Group</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Dalian" title="Port of Dalian">Dalian Port</a> is an important port for international trade. It has established trading and shipping links with more than 300 ports in 160 countries and regions of the world. There are over 100 international and domestic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Containerisation" title="Containerisation">container shipping</a> routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-port_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-port-43">[43]</a></sup> A harbor for oil tankers (the largest by tonnage in China),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-port_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-port-43">[43]</a></sup> at the terminus of an oil <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_transport" title="Pipeline transport">pipeline</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daqing_oilfields" title="Daqing oilfields">Daqing oilfields</a>, was completed in 1976. Dalian is the 6th largest port in China;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and according to <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Port_Authorities" title="American Association of Port Authorities">AAPA</a> world port ranking data, Dalian is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_ports_by_cargo_tonnage" title="List of world's busiest ports by cargo tonnage">8th busiest port</a> in the world by cargo tonnage in 2012, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_container_ports" title="List of world's busiest container ports">12th busiest container port</a> in the world by total number of <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">TEUs</a> handled in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Accordingly, Dalian is a major center for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_refineries" title="Oil refineries">oil refineries</a>, diesel engineering, and chemical production.</p>
<p>Also completed in 1993 is a newer port called Dàyáowān Port (大窑湾港), on Dàgūshān (大孤山) Peninsula in the northern suburbs, specialising in import-export of mining and oil products. Together with the <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Railway_Station" title="Dalian Railway Station">Dalian Railway Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalian_North_Railway_Station" title="Dalian North Railway Station">Dalian North Railway Station</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalian_International_Airport" title="Dalian International Airport">Dalian International Airport</a> and two major express roads to <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenda_Expressway" title="Shenda Expressway">Shenda Expressway</a>), <a href="/wiki/Changchun" title="Changchun">Changchun</a> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Changda_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Changda Expressway (page does not exist)">Changda Expressway</a>), <a href="/wiki/Harbin" title="Harbin">Harbin</a> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hada_Expressway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hada Expressway (page does not exist)">Hada Expressway</a>) in the north and to <a href="/wiki/Dandong" title="Dandong">Dandong</a> to the east, Dalian has been an important distribution centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xinghai_CBD.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Xinghai_CBD.JPG/220px-Xinghai_CBD.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Xinghai_CBD.JPG/330px-Xinghai_CBD.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Xinghai_CBD.JPG/440px-Xinghai_CBD.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="thumb tright">

</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_zones">Industrial zones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Industrial zones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dalian_Development_Zone" title="Dalian Development Zone">Dalian Development Zone</a></div>
<p>Dalian has been given many benefits by the Chinese government, including the title of "open-city" (1984), which allows it to receive considerable <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign investment</a> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of the People's Republic of China">Special Economic Zone</a>). The Development Zone was established in Jinzhou District, to which many Japanese companies, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canon_(company)" title="Canon (company)">Canon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Electric" title="Mitsubishi Electric">Mitsubishi Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nidec" title="Nidec">Nidec</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanyo_Electric" title="Sanyo Electric">Sanyo Electric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a>, followed by South Korean, American and European companies (such as <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a>). In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> announced plans to build a semiconductor fabrication facility (commonly known as a fab) in the Development Zone, Dalian. It is Intel's first fab to be built at an entirely new site since 1992. The facility began operation in October 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Dalian also houses auto-manufacturing plants for <a href="/wiki/Chery" title="Chery">Chery</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dongfeng_Motor#Dongfeng_Nissan" title="Dongfeng Motor">Dongfeng Nissan</a> Passenger Vehicle Company,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BYD_Automobile" title="BYD Automobile">BYD Automobile</a> (a production base for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BYD_electric_bus" title="BYD electric bus">BYD K9 electric buses</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other zones in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Development_Area" title="Dalian Development Area">Dalian Economic and Technological Development Zone</a>, Dalian Export Processing Zone, Dalian Free Trade Zone, and <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Hi-Tech_Zone" title="Dalian Hi-Tech Zone">Dalian Hi-Tech Industrial Zone</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_and_IT_industry">Financial and IT industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Financial and IT industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Hi-Tech_Zone" title="Dalian Hi-Tech Zone">Dalian Hi-Tech Zone</a></div>
<p>Dalian is the financial centre of <a href="/wiki/Northeast_China" title="Northeast China">Northeast China</a>. There are the Dalian branches of China's five major banks: <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_China" title="Bank of China">Bank of China</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_%26_Commercial_Bank_of_China" title="Industrial &amp; Commercial Bank of China">Industrial &amp; Commercial Bank of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Construction_Bank" title="China Construction Bank">China Construction Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Communications" title="Bank of Communications">Bank of Communications</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_Bank_of_China" title="Agricultural Bank of China">Agricultural Bank of China</a>. Dalian City Commercial Bank is now called <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Dalian" title="Bank of Dalian">Bank of Dalian</a>, which among other things handles processing of the Dalian Mingzhu IC Card for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transportation" title="Public transportation">public transportation</a>. Bank of Dalian has opened branches in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a>, among five other cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Founded in 1993, <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Commodity_Exchange" title="Dalian Commodity Exchange">Dalian Commodity Exchange</a> (DCE) is the only <a href="/wiki/Futures_exchange" title="Futures exchange">futures exchange</a> in Northeast China. The futures industry leaped forward in its development. Among its 16 listed futures products approved by the <a href="/wiki/China_Securities_Regulatory_Commission" title="China Securities Regulatory Commission">China Securities Regulatory Commission</a> (CSRC) are corn, corn starch, soybeans, soybean meal, soybean oil, RBD palm olein, <a href="/wiki/Linear_low-density_polyethylene" title="Linear low-density polyethylene">linear low-density polyethylene</a> (LLDPE), <a href="/wiki/Polyvinyl_chloride" title="Polyvinyl chloride">polyvinyl chloride</a> (PVC), <a href="/wiki/Polypropylene" title="Polypropylene">polypropylene</a> (PP), coke, coking coal, iron ore, egg, fiberboard and blockboard. In 2014, DCE achieved 770 million lots and RMB 41.5 trillion respectively in trading volume and turnover. According to the <a href="/wiki/Futures_Industry_Association" title="Futures Industry Association">Futures Industry Association</a> (FIA) of the U.S., DCE ranked the 10th out of the global leading derivative exchanges in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the 1990s, Dalian has emphasized the development of the IT industry, especially in <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Hi-Tech_Zone" title="Dalian Hi-Tech Zone">Dalian Hi-Tech Zone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Software_Park" title="Dalian Software Park">Dalian Software Park</a> in the western suburbs near <a href="/wiki/Dalian_University_of_Technology" title="Dalian University of Technology">Dalian University of Technology</a>. Dalian High-Tech Zone is the base of high-tech industries, housing more than 4,700 enterprises, including 80 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-high_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-high-54">[54]</a></sup> Not only Chinese IT companies, such as <a href="/wiki/Dalian_Hi-Think_Computer" title="Dalian Hi-Think Computer">DHC</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HiSoft_Technology_International" title="HiSoft Technology International">Hisoft</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neusoft_Group" title="Neusoft Group">Neusoft Group</a>, but also American, European, Indian and Japanese IT companies are located there, including <a href="/wiki/Infosys" title="Infosys">Infosys</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dell" title="Dell">Dell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">HP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hitachi" title="Hitachi">Hitachi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cisco" title="Cisco">Cisco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-high_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-high-54">[54]</a></sup> Nine professional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Business_incubators" title="Business incubators">business incubators</a> are also located in the area, including the Hi-tech Business Incubator, animation and software incubators, with over 400 companies incubated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-high_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-high-54">[54]</a></sup> Currently, the "<a href="/wiki/Lushun_South_Road" title="Lushun South Road">Lüshun South Road</a> Software Industry Belt" Plan is proceeding, including Dalian Software Park Phase 3.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_Intel_manufacturing_sites#Fab_sites" title="List of Intel manufacturing sites">Fab 68</a> is located in Dalian. The plan was announced on 26 March 2007, and operations started on 26 October 2010. It is Intel's first chip-manufacturing fabrication in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xinghai_square_middle.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Xinghai_square_middle.JPG/220px-Xinghai_square_middle.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Xinghai_square_middle.JPG/330px-Xinghai_square_middle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Xinghai_square_middle.JPG/440px-Xinghai_square_middle.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xinghai_square_middle.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Xinghai_Square" title="Xinghai Square">Xinghai Square</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_city_squares_by_size" title="List of city squares by size">largest city square in the world</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dalian is a popular destination among domestic tourists and foreign visitors, especially from Japan, South Korea and Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shp_10-8"><a href="#cite_note-shp-10">[10]</a></sup> Its mild climate and multiple beaches as well as its importance in the modern history of China have attracted tourists. Some of the most famous beaches are Jīnshítān Golden Coast (<span lang="zh-Hans">金石滩黄金海岸</span>) beach, Fùjiāzhuāng (<span lang="zh">付家庄</span>) beach, Bàngchuídǎo (<span lang="zh">棒棰岛</span>) beach, Xīnghǎi Park (<span lang="zh">星海公园</span>) beach, Xīnghǎi Bay (<span lang="zh">星海湾</span>) beach, and Xiàjiāhézi (<span lang="zh">夏家河子</span>) beach. In 2007, it was one of the three cities named "China's best tourist city", along with <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>, recognized by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Tourism_Administration" title="National Tourism Administration">National Tourism Administration</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_World_Tourism_Organization" title="United Nations World Tourism Organization">United Nations World Tourism Organization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xinghai_Square_west.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Xinghai_Square_west.JPG/220px-Xinghai_Square_west.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Xinghai_Square_west.JPG/330px-Xinghai_Square_west.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Xinghai_Square_west.JPG/440px-Xinghai_Square_west.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Grand Hyatt Dalian (left) and apartments at <a href="/wiki/Xinghai_Square" title="Xinghai Square">Xinghai Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four_inner-city_districts">Four inner-city districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Four inner-city districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Square_(Dalian)" title="Zhongshan Square (Dalian)">Zhongshan Square</a></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Originally designed by Russians in the 19th century, Zhongshan Square (中山广场) is especially noted for the <a href="/wiki/Modern_Buildings_on_Zhongshan_Square_in_Dalian" title="Modern Buildings on Zhongshan Square in Dalian">several classical buildings</a> located around the square built during the first half of the 20th century by the Japanese.</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Laohutan Ocean Park: the park contains the Polar Region Marine Animals World,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laohutan_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-laohutan-57">[57]</a></sup> the Coral Aquarium, and the World of Birds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laohutan_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-laohutan-57">[57]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_whale" title="White whale">white whale</a> and dolphin show is a major attraction in the Polar Region Marine Animals World.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The Tigers Sculpture Square is nearby, whose tiger sculpture is the symbol of Tiger Beach (<span lang="zh-Hans">老虎滩</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Lǎohǔtān</span></i>). A retired <a href="/wiki/Anshan-class_destroyer" title="Anshan-class destroyer"><i>Anshan</i>-class destroyer</a> <i>Taiyuan</i> is open to visitors.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG/220px-Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG/330px-Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG/440px-Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dalian_Laohutan_Ocean_Park.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dalian Laohutan Ocean Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xinghai_Square" title="Xinghai Square">Xinghai Square</a>: situated at the Xinghai Bay, Xinghai Square (<span lang="zh-Hans">星海广场</span>; "Square of the Sea of Stars") was built at the centennial of the City of Dalian (1998) and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_city_squares_by_size" title="List of city squares by size">largest city square in the world</a>.</li>
<li>Hēishíjiāo Geological Park and Dalian Natural History Museum</li>
<li>Sunasia Ocean World</li>
<li>Dalian Forest Zoo</li>
<li>Bangchuidao Scenic Area: a well-maintained park used as a State Guesthouse since 1960, the Bangchuidao Scenic Area is now open to the public with upgraded features including lavish greens, Chinese and western style villas, hot spring, tennis courts, badminton courts, a recreation center, a golf course and the Bangchuidao beach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The Bangchui Island (<span lang="zh-Hans">棒棰岛</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Bàngchuí Dǎo</span></i>, named for an <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islet</a> in the shape of an ancient washing tool Bangchui)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> can be seen from the beach. As a State Guesthouse, the scenic area has received numerous Chinese and foreign leaders and high profile officials, including <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Zemin" title="Jiang Zemin">Jiang Zemin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">Henry Kissinger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Schr%C3%B6der" title="Gerhard Schröder">Gerhard Schröder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Samaranch" title="Juan Antonio Samaranch">Juan Antonio Samaranch</a> and so on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
